\#\# \*\*PHASE 1: THE STAGE IS SET (18:47:33 \- 18:49:12)\*\*

\*\*\[DRONE SHOT \- Overhead Recon\]\*\*

Summit of Mt. Takatsuki. Node 1 dominates the center—forty-meter antenna array, humming with that deep frequency that makes your teeth ache. Three relay towers arranged in perfect triangle formation, each pulsing with synchronized light. Wind at 15-20 kph, rocky terrain, dusk bleeding into night.

Target CIPHER stands near the primary antenna. Distinctive silhouette: athletic build, backpack apparatus with two uneven antennas (3ft and 5ft) swaying like reeds. Three PLA personnel in formation nearby, movements aberrant—puppet-stutters, joints at wrong angles.

Subject SHADE crests the final approach path at 18:47:41.

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

I see him before he speaks. Standing there like he's been waiting. Like this is a stage and I'm late for my entrance.

I pull down the Glassigs. \*\*Click-hummmmm.\*\* The world shifts to thermal. Node reads white-hot. The three soldiers glow orange, but wrong—their heat signatures pulse in unison. Then I see them: thin lines of warmth connecting Cipher's backpack to each soldier's spine.

Wires. Strings. Whatever the fuck you want to call them.

\*\*\[AUDIO LOG \- 18:47:58\]\*\*

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* \*(turning slowly, theatrical)\* "Ah. Right on time. I've been watching your ascent, you know. Very determined. Very... scripted."

\*\*SHADE:\*\* "Let them go."

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* \*(laughing softly)\* "Let them go? My friend, they've already \*gone\*. The question is: where? And the answer—" \*(spreads arms, backpack antennas spark)\* "—is exactly where they needed to be. We're all playing our parts tonight. This is the climax. The moment where the protagonist confronts the antagonist, yes? Very dramatic. I do love theater."

\*\*SHADE:\*\* "You're insane."

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "No, no. I'm \*enlightened\*. There's a difference. Insanity is fighting the script. Enlightenment is \*writing\* it. Or better yet—letting it write you."

\*\*\[SHADE'S ACCOUNT\]\*\*

\- Target confirmed at 18:47:51

\- Three hostiles, puppeted (thermal wiring visible via SIG-H)

\- Cipher's demeanor: theatrical, confident, \*rehearsed\*

\- Psychological assessment: He'd been preparing this speech

\- Environmental factors: wind, rocky terrain, node interference causing periodic Glassigs flicker

\- Initial impression: This wasn't going to be a normal fight

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

The first soldier jerks forward. His face—I zoom in with the Glassigs. Twenty-two, maybe. Chinese features, scared eyes. 

His eyes are \*moving\* independently of his body. Tracking me while his limbs puppet-stutter into combat stance. And for just a second, our gazes lock.

I see him understand what's about to happen.

That look. Like standing at a cliff's edge. That split-second where your body knows you're going to jump or fall, and there's nothing you can do but \*feel\* the adrenaline and terror and absolute certainty of what comes next.

Then his body moves, and his eyes don't follow.

\*\*\[AUDIO LOG \- 18:48:22\]\*\*

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "You see it, don't you? That awareness. Beautiful, isn't it? He knows. He feels everything. The difference is—" \*(antennas hum louder)\* "—he doesn't have to \*choose\* anymore. I've lifted that burden. Every puppet dreams of freedom, Shade. But what we really want? Better strings. Invisible ones. That never tangle. That feel like \*choice\*."

\*\*SHADE:\*\* "That's not—"

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "Not what? Not natural? Not \*right\*?" \*(smiles)\* "Who told you that? Your training? Your culture? Your precious Western individualism? All scripts, my friend. I'm just honest about mine."

\*\*\[SHADE'S ACCOUNT\]\*\*

\- Engagement initiated 18:48:31

\- Attempted non-lethal protocols

\- Adjusted tactics: disable, don't kill

\- Psychological note: Cipher talks. A lot. It's a tactic—keeping me off-balance.

\- Secondary note: It's working.

\---

\#\# \*\*PHASE 2: THE PHANTOM WIRE (18:49:13 \- 18:51:47)\*\*

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

I move left, trying to flank toward the first relay tower. Two puppets intercept—synchronized, inhuman precision. The third hangs back, rifle trained.

I'm trading blows with the first when Cipher's voice carries across the summit:

\*\*\[AUDIO LOG \- 18:49:44\]\*\*

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "Middle child, yes? I did my research. Middle children are \*fascinating\*. Always balancing. Always mediating. Big brother's ambition, little brother's chaos, and you—" \*(sound of electrical spark)\* "—holding the center. Tell me, Shade. Don't you ever get tired of being the glue?"

\*\*SHADE:\*\* \*(breathing hard, dodging)\* "Shut up."

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "That's what I thought. You know what's exhausting? Being a \*person\*. Having to decide, every second, who you are. What you want. What you believe. I'm offering \*rest\*."

\*\*\[SHADE'S ACCOUNT\]\*\*

\- He kept talking through the entire engagement

\- Not random commentary—targeted psychological warfare

\- He knew things about me. About my brothers.

\- Had to compartmentalize. Focus on the fight.

\- Easier said than done.

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

I'm pinned. Two puppets boxing me in, the third has his rifle raised. I watch his finger tighten on the trigger—his finger, his gun, but not his \*choice\*.

Then: \*\*CRACK.\*\*

His head snaps back. Clean shot. He drops.

I don't have time to process. Second shot—relay tower R1 explodes in a shower of sparks and metal shrapnel. The puppet to my left collapses instantly, strings cut.

My Glassigs crackle. Static. Then a voice I don't recognize:

\*\*\[AUDIO \- UNIDENTIFIED FEMALE\]:\*\* "Keep moving."

\*\*\[SHADE'S ACCOUNT\]\*\*

\- Unknown ally, sniper-class, extreme precision

\- R1 neutralized at 18:50:36

\- Puppet count: 2 remaining

\- Questions multiplying faster than answers:

  \- Who is she?

  \- How does she know where I am?

  \- Can I trust her?

\- Answer: Doesn't matter. She just saved my life.

\*\*\[DRONE SHOT\]\*\*

CIPHER's backpack antennas spark wildly. Brief loss of composure. Recovers quickly, antennas stabilize. Remaining two hostiles move with increased aggression.

\*\*\[AUDIO LOG \- 18:50:52\]\*\*

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* \*(laughing, delighted)\* "Oh, wonderful\\\! \*Guests\*\\\! The plot thickens. You know what this is giving? Main character energy. For real for real."

\*(pause)\*

"But here's the thing about protagonists, Shade. They think they're making choices. Writing their own story. But the author's already decided how it ends."

\*\*\[SHADE'S ACCOUNT\]\*\*

\- That phrase: "main character energy"

\- Delivered with zero enthusiasm

\- Like he was reading from a script

\- Made my skin crawl more than anything else he'd said

\- Because he meant it literally

\---

\#\# \*\*PHASE 3: THE CHAOS VARIABLE (18:51:48 \- 18:53:29)\*\*

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

Moving toward R2. Two puppets left, fighting harder now. More desperate. One tackles me and I feel his body \*trembling\*—not exertion, \*resistance\*. He's trying to stop. Can't.

Cipher continues his performance:

\*\*\[AUDIO LOG \- 18:52:11\]\*\*

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "Do you know what I loved about Chinese philosophy? Not the government—please, let's not be crude. I mean the \*old\* texts. The idea that selfhood is \*relational\*. That you're not a single 'you,' but a web of connections. In the West, you worship the lonely individual. But you know what individuals are? \*Separated\*. In pain. Screaming into the void."

\*\*SHADE:\*\* "And your solution is to make everyone puppets?"

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "My solution is to make the connections \*visible\*. Undeniable. You think I'm controlling them? I'm removing the \*illusion\* of separation. They're not alone anymore. Neither am I. We're all part of the same—"

\*\*\[DRONE SHOT \- TIMESTAMP ANOMALY\]\*\*

At 18:52:44, equipment malfunction near node structure. Civilian-sized figure briefly visible before taking cover. Appears accidental. Power surge. R2 relay tower goes dark.

One hostile collapses immediately.

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

The tower sparks out. Second puppet drops like someone cut his strings.

Because someone did.

Bonta. Has to be. That kid's chaos manifesting at exactly the right moment.

Cipher's antennas hum louder—I can hear them over the wind, over the node, over my own heartbeat.

\*\*\[AUDIO LOG \- 18:52:51\]\*\*

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* \*(still smiling)\* "Chaos. My favorite variable. See, that's what makes this \*interesting\*. If it was all scripted, it wouldn't be art. The unpredictability—the \*accident\*—that's what makes the performance \*real\*."

\*\*\[SHADE'S ACCOUNT\]\*\*

\- Single puppet remaining

\- Cipher's composure: cracking but \*performing\* the crack

\- Everything is theater to him

\- Even his own defeat would be theater

\- That should've warned me

\---

\#\# \*\*PHASE 4: THE WIRE SNAP (18:53:30 \- 18:55:08)\*\*

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

The last soldier is fighting with suicidal aggression. No self-preservation. All offense. Cipher's pushing the limit, seeing how far the dial can turn before the puppet breaks.

I realize: he's not just controlling them. He's \*amplifying\* what's already there. Fear. Obedience. Desperation. Taking the volume from 3 to 11\.

\*\*\[AUDIO LOG \- 18:53:47\]\*\*

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* \*(stepping closer, antennas glowing)\* "You feel it, don't you? That pull. That \*wire\*. We're not so different, you and me."

\*\*SHADE:\*\* "I'm nothing like you."

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "No? You burn energy to break physics. I burn energy to break \*wills\*. Same enhancement. Same source. Same... \*family\*."

\*(He pauses, lets that word hang)\*

\*\*SHADE:\*\* "What?"

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "Oh, you don't know yet. Of course you don't. But \*he\* does. I spoke with one of your brothers, Shade. Had a lovely conversation. And he understood. He \*saw\* the strings. Felt the relief of admitting they were there."

\*\*SHADE:\*\* "You're lying."

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "Am I? Or are you just afraid I'm not?"

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

I check my Exposure meter. It's fluctuating. Patterns that don't match my Dare usage.

I think: \*Am I being puppeted right now?\*

And then I think: \*How would I know?\*

\*\*\[AUDIO LOG \- 18:54:29\]\*\*

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "That doubt. Right there. That's the \*tug\*. The moment you wonder: am I choosing this? Or am I being chosen? And here's the secret, Shade—" \*(antennas hum so loud the drone footage distorts)\* "—it doesn't matter. The question itself is the wire. You'll never know. And that uncertainty? That's the real prison."

\*\*SHADE:\*\* \*(quiet)\* "Shut up."

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "Make me."

\*\*\[SHADE'S ACCOUNT\]\*\*

\- Psychological warfare: devastatingly effective

\- He'd gotten in my head completely

\- One of my brothers had talked to him

\- Which one? Sun? Scorch?

\- When?

\- Tactical decision: end this \*now\* before I lose myself completely

\- Emotional state: compromised but functional (lying to myself)

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

I feint toward R3. Cipher tracks me. Puppet intercepts.

I pivot.

"Wire Snap."

\*\*\[SYSTEM READOUT\]\*\*

\`\`\`

DARE ACTIVATION: 糸切り (ITO-KIRI) / WIRE SNAP

ENERGY COST: 34%

EXPOSURE SPIKE: \+42 units

STATUS: CRITICAL THRESHOLD APPROACHING

EFFECT: CONNECTION DISRUPTION \- SINGLE TARGET

DURATION: INSTANTANEOUS

\`\`\`

\*\*\[DRONE SHOT\]\*\*

Subject SHADE's hands emit sharp luminescence. Performs severing gesture—precise, violent. Thermal wiring between CIPHER and remaining hostile becomes visible to standard optical spectrum.

\[NOTE: This should not be possible. Multiple analysts have confirmed: the wires appear on standard video feed at timestamp 18:54:53. Recommend investigation.\]

The wires \*snap\* audibly. \*\*TWANG-crack-twang.\*\*

Hostile collapses to knees. Immediate physiological relief response visible.

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

The soldier drops. Free. His eyes clear—actually \*clear\*, like waking from a nightmare. He looks at his hands. Flexes his fingers. His own fingers. His own \*choice\*.

He looks at me.

That moment before the jump. But this time, he's standing on solid ground, realizing he didn't fall.

He doesn't thank me. Just scrambles away, limping, free, \*his\*.

Cipher stands alone now. Backpack sparking. Antennas bending at wrong angles.

I advance.

\*\*\[AUDIO LOG \- 18:54:58\]\*\*

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "You think you freed him? You just gave him back the \*weight\*. Now he has to choose. Has to decide. Has to be \*separate\* again."

\*(He's backing up, but smiling)\*

"That's not mercy, Shade. That's cruelty. Every puppet wants better strings. I gave him \*perfect\* strings. And you cut them."

\*\*SHADE:\*\* "He's free."

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* "He's \*alone\*. There's a difference."

\---

\#\# \*\*PHASE 5: TRANSCENDENCE (18:55:09 \- 18:55:43)\*\*

\*\*\[AUDIO LOG \- 18:55:14\]\*\*

\*\*CIPHER:\*\* \*(backing toward cliff edge)\* "Well. Shit."

\*(Forced laugh. It cracks halfway through.)\*

"You know what? I prepared for this outcome too. Every good performance needs an ending. Even if it's... \*premature\*."

\*(Looks directly at camera)\*

"Toodle-oo, I guess."

\*\*\[SHADE'S ACCOUNT\]\*\*

\- That line wasn't playful

\- It was \*terrified\*

\- I hit him—careful strike, meant to incapacitate

\- He went down

\- And then...

\- Then it got strange

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

I hear it before I see it.

\*\*Whirr-click-whirr.\*\*

Mechanical. Precise. \*Purposeful.\*

Black drone descends from above. Eight segmented legs, each ending in surgical implements. About the size of a large dog. Moving with the efficiency of something that's done this before.

I see the markings.

\*\*USSFDOA.\*\*

United States Space Force Department of Otherworldly Affairs.

American. Our side. \*My\* side.

\*\*\[DRONE SHOT \- EXTERNAL SURVEILLANCE\]\*\*

Unidentified recovery unit (designation: HARVEST-class) descends at 18:55:21. Design consistent with neural extraction protocols. Targets fallen CIPHER operative. Ignores SHADE entirely.

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

The drone's legs pin his head. Eight points of contact. Medical precision.

Cipher's still conscious. Eyes wide. He tries to speak but can't—jaw locked by the drone's grip.

Blade deploys.

Clean incision along cranial suture line. \*\*Ssssshhhk-crack.\*\*

I should look away.

I don't.

\*\*\[SHADE'S ACCOUNT\]\*\*

\- Duration: 20 seconds from landing to extraction

\- Clinical. Surgical. Practiced.

\- Cipher's eyes stayed open the entire time

\- Locked on mine

\- No fear in them

\- Just... \*satisfaction\*

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

The drone removes his brain. Preservation chamber deploys—transparent, filled with oxygenated fluid. I watch the brain \*pulse\* as it's transferred.

Cipher's eyes don't blink. Don't move. But they're still \*looking\* at me.

And I swear—I \*swear\*—in that moment, I hear his voice in my head:

\*See? I told you. Better strings. Invisible ones.\*

But that's impossible. His vocal cords are still in his body. His mouth isn't moving.

\*\*\[SHADE'S ACCOUNT\]\*\*

\- Brain extraction complete: 18:55:38

\- Preservation chamber sealed

\- Drone departed: 18:55:41

\- Body left intact, head cavity open, eyes still staring

\- Questions (incomplete list):

  \- Why American tech?

  \- Why harvest the brain?  

  \- Why leave the body?

  \- What did "we're already connected" mean?

  \- Which brother did he speak to?

  \- Why was this fight so... \*easy\*?

  \- Am I being puppeted right now?

  \- How would I know?

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

I stand there. Breathing hard. Exposure meter screaming critical. But I'm barely injured.

Three puppets. Three towers. One Champion operative.

Should've been harder.

\*Was\* I puppeted? Did she—whoever that sniper was—do all the work?

Did Bonta's accident save me?

Did Cipher \*let\* me win?

I look at his body. Eyes still open, fixed on the sky. That satisfied smile frozen on his face.

The node hums behind me. Continuous. Indifferent. It doesn't care who won.

Somewhere in the dark: voices. Movement. Other people arriving.

But I'm alone with questions I can't answer.

\*\*\[AUDIO LOG \- 18:55:49 \- UNIDENTIFIED TRANSMISSION\]\*\*

\*\*UNKNOWN VOICE:\*\* "Target secure. Node 1 compromised. Extract recommended."

Static. The voice wasn't talking to me.

Wasn't even on my frequency.

\*\*\[BODY CAM \- SHADE\]\*\*

I turn away from Cipher's corpse. The node's humming follows me as I descend.

In my peripheral vision, I see movement. Figures emerging from cover. Bonta. Maybe the sniper.

But I don't stop.

Because Cipher's last words loop in my head:

\*Every puppet wants better strings. I gave him perfect strings. And you cut them.\*

And I think: What if he's right?

What if freedom is just another word for being alone?

What if the strings were always there?

\*\*\[SYSTEM READOUT \- FINAL\]\*\*

\`\`\`

MISSION STATUS: OBJECTIVE COMPLETE

CIPHER OPERATIVE: NEUTRALIZED

NODE 1: COMPROMISED

EXPOSURE LEVEL: 89% (CRITICAL \- IMMEDIATE REST REQUIRED)

PSYCHOLOGICAL EVALUATION: PENDING

\`\`\`

\*\*\[END REPORT \- 18:56:02\]\*\*

\---

\#\# \*\*\[ARCHIVIST'S NOTE \- 2037\]\*\*

I've reviewed this footage forty-three times.

Three observations:

\*\*First:\*\* The "thermal wires" become visible to standard cameras at 18:54:53. This violates every principle of how the Glassigs work. Yet multiple analysts confirm: they're there. On \*video\*. Visible to anyone watching.

\*\*Second:\*\* Cipher's expression at moment of extraction (18:55:34-38) registers as: \*satisfaction\*. Facial recognition software reads it as genuine. Not fear. Not pain. \*Relief\*.

\*\*Third:\*\* The drone's markings are authentic. Serial number traces to Kadena Air Base, PROJECT HARVEST MOON. When I requested further details, my clearance was revoked for 72 hours. Someone doesn't want us asking about those drones.

Shade's question remains: Why was it easy?

I have a theory.

Cipher didn't lose the fight. He lost the argument. And decided that was victory enough.

Because now Shade will spend the rest of his life wondering: \*Am I choosing this? Or am I being chosen?\*

That doubt. That uncertainty.

That's the \*tug\*.

And once you feel it, you never stop.

The puppet who cuts his own strings.

Except the strings were never external.

They were always internal.

And Cipher knew.

He always knew.

—\*Archivist Ma, April 2037\*

\*\[Personal note, handwritten:\]\*  

\*Watched the extraction again today. Cipher's eyes at the moment the blade touches skull—they don't show fear. They show\* recognition\*. Like he's seeing something he'd been promised. Something he'd\* wanted\*.\*

\*What did they promise him?\*  

\*What did they promise Sun?\*

\*I'm afraid we already know.\*

\---

\*\*END CHAPTER 8\*\*

## \# \*\*Shade's Journal \- Node 1 Encounter\*\*

\*\*Date: \[REDACTED\]\*\*  

\*\*Location: Mt. Takatsuki Summit, Zamami Island\*\*  

\*\*Time: Approximately 19:15 Hours (I think—time's been weird since the extraction)\*\*

\---

I need to write this down while it's still fresh. Before I convince myself it was something else. Before exhaustion rewrites the memory into something safer.

Her name is Timeera Koi.

I know that because she told me. Eventually.

\---

I was still standing over Cipher's body when I felt it—that pressure change in the air. The one that came right before the drone descended. But different this time. Quieter. Like the island was taking a breath.

I turned toward the treeline.

The forest had been dead still. That mean silence Bonta wrote about in his diary, the kind that makes your ears strain. But now the branches were moving. Not from wind. They were \*parting\*. Opening.

Like something was walking through and the trees were getting out of the fucking way.

I blinked. Rubbed my eyes. Exposure meter still screaming critical—maybe I was hallucinating. Maybe the Wire Snap had cost me more than I thought.

But the trees kept moving.

And then she stepped out.

No vehicle. No announcement. Just walked out of that dark forest like she'd been taking an evening stroll. Rifle slung over one shoulder, moving with the kind of confidence that comes from being exactly where you're supposed to be.

The trees settled behind her. Closed ranks. Like nothing had happened.

I stared at the forest. Then at her. Then back at the forest.

"Did the trees just—"

"Did they?" She smiled. Not mocking. Something else. Like she was letting me in on a joke I hadn't learned the punchline to yet.

I wanted to ask. Wanted to know if I'd really seen what I thought I'd seen, if the island was playing tricks, if Cipher's philosophy was bleeding into reality.

But the question died because she was walking toward me now, and I got my first real look:

Mixed—Black and Asian, I think. Early thirties, maybe thirty-three, thirty-four. Hair pulled back in a tight bun, a few strands loose around her face. Tactical gear, dark blue, almost black in the failing light. Form-fitting doesn't do it justice. The gear was \*designed\* to move, but it was also designed to be noticed. 

She was built solid. Not thin. Curves that the tactical suit didn't hide—accentuated them, actually. And the neckline was unzipped. Not all the way. Just enough.

I tried to focus on her face. Failed. She noticed.

That smile again. Satisfied.

"Shade," she said. Not a question. She knew who I was, knew I'd be here, probably knew what I'd been thinking for the last thirty seconds.

I should've established control. Should've asked who she was, what she wanted, why she'd helped. Instead:

"Nice shot."

She laughed. Actually laughed, and it sounded genuine. "You're welcome. Most people say thank you when someone saves their life."

"Thank you."

"Better." She stopped about three meters away. Close enough to talk without shouting, far enough that I'd have to close the distance if I wanted to. "You look like shit, by the way."

"Just fought a puppeteer and watched a drone harvest his brain. It's been a day."

"I noticed. The fight, I mean. Good use of Wire Snap. Textbook severance technique."

"You know about—"

"About the Dare system? About your enhancements? About why American drones are extracting Champion-class brains?" She tilted her head. "I know a lot of things, Shade. Question is: are you ready to hear them?"

And just like that, she had control of the conversation.

I spent the next twenty minutes trying to get it back.

Spoiler: I didn't.

\---

\#\# \*\*What She Told Me (In Order, Because I Need to Remember This Exactly)\*\*

\*\*First:\*\* The node isn't fully disabled. What I did to Cipher stopped the immediate puppeting, knocked down his control network, but the main antenna array is still broadcasting. Still "listening." She used that word—listening—like the node was alive.

\*\*Second:\*\* There are seven nodes total. Seven islands across Okinawa Prefecture. She wouldn't say which islands, but from the way she said it, they're already active. Or close.

\*\*Third:\*\* "The nodes aren't what your command told you they are."

I asked what they actually were.

She stepped closer. Close enough that I could smell her—sweat, gun oil, something else underneath. Not perfume. Just her.

(I'm writing this detail down because I need to remember: she \*chose\* to step closer. This was tactical. This was a move.)

"They're a frequency," she said. "Broadcasting at a level that makes you forget you have a choice. You think you're deciding, but you're just responding to the signal. Cipher was a test case—one person, one backpack, limited range. These?" She gestured at the forty-meter antenna array humming behind us. "Cover an entire island. Maybe more."

"So it's mass puppeting."

"No. It's worse than that." She held my gaze. "Puppeting is obvious. You know you're being controlled. This is \*subtle\*. You still think you're choosing. You just don't realize the options were always limited. Like..." She paused, searching for the metaphor. "Like scrolling through a feed. You think you're deciding what to click, but the algorithm already decided what you'd see."

\*\*Fourth:\*\* She knows about my brothers.

I didn't bring them up. She did.

"One of them is looking for you," she said, casual, like she was commenting on the weather. "The other one... he's looking for something else."

My chest tightened. "Which is which?"

"You'll figure it out."

"That's not an answer."

"It's the only one you're getting. For now."

"How do you even—have you \*talked\* to them?"

She smiled. Not the satisfied smile from before. This one was almost sympathetic. Almost.

"I've talked to one of them. Had a very interesting conversation, actually. He understands more than you do. About the nodes. About what you are."

"What \*we\* are?"

"There it is. The question you should've asked first." She turned, started walking toward the node's base. "Come on. I'll show you how to shut this thing down properly. And then we need to leave."

\---

\#\# \*\*The Node (Technical Shit I Need to Remember)\*\*

There's a control terminal at the base of each antenna array. Military-grade encryption, but she had bypass codes. Rattled them off like a phone number: twenty-six characters, alphanumeric, that I immediately committed to memory because I needed \*something\* to focus on besides the way she leaned over the terminal.

The short version:

1\. Physical access to the base terminal

2\. Input bypass sequence

3\. Initiate hard shutdown protocol

4\. Node goes dark, frequency stops broadcasting

"What happens to the people who were under influence?" I asked.

"The ones Cipher was directly puppeting? They'll recover. Disoriented, traumatized, but themselves." She didn't look up from the terminal. "The ones who've been under the node's ambient influence for weeks? We'll find out."

"That's not reassuring."

"It's not supposed to be."

She pulled a data stick from her vest—and yes, I noticed where it had been tucked—and handed it to me. "Codes for Nodes 2 through 7 are on here. Encrypted. You'll need them."

"Why are you giving this to me?"

"Because I need you alive. For now."

"For now?"

That smile. The dangerous one. "Motivation, Shade. It's what separates you from Cipher's puppets. Keep wondering why I'm helping, and you'll keep moving."

I took the data stick. Our fingers brushed. Barely. She held the contact for exactly one second longer than necessary.

I'm writing this down so I remember: \*she held it\*.

\---

\#\# \*\*The Part Where I Realize I'm Being Played (And It Doesn't Help)\*\*

I know what a honeypot operation looks like. I've been briefed. Attractive operative uses sexuality as a weapon, gets you to drop your guard, extracts information or manipulates behavior.

Knowing that didn't help.

Because here's the thing: she was obvious about it. The way she moved, the way she stood, the way she looked at me—it wasn't subtle. It was a performance. And she knew I knew it was a performance.

And I was still affected.

That's what Cipher meant. The tug. The wire you can see but can't escape.

I tried to focus on the tactical situation. On the questions I needed answers to. Where are my brothers. What are the nodes really for. Why is American tech harvesting Champion brains.

But part of my brain—the part that hadn't slept in two days, that had just burned through half my Exposure limit, that was still hearing Cipher's voice saying \*we're already connected\*—that part was cataloging different things.

The way she moved. The way the tactical gear shifted when she reached up to adjust something on the terminal. The curve of her neck when she tilted her head.

She was watching me the same way I'd watched Cipher's puppets. Cataloging. Calculating.

The difference: I wasn't sure I minded.

And that scared me more than the brain-harvesting drone.

\---

\#\# \*\*Oh, and Bonta Was There\*\*

Kid showed up about halfway through the node explanation. Stumbled out of the rocks looking like he'd just survived an earthquake. Burned arm rewrapped—better than before, actually. Someone had dressed it properly.

Timeera glanced at him once. "Friend of yours?"

"Not really. Local kid. Got caught up in things."

"Huh." She turned back to the terminal. "He should leave the island. Soon as possible. This place is about to get worse."

Bonta didn't say much after that. Just stood there, shifting his weight, clearly trying to figure out if he should leave or stay or what. Eventually he settled on "stay but stay twenty feet away and don't make noise."

Smart kid.

\---

\#\# \*\*What Happened Next (The Part I'm Still Trying to Process)\*\*

We were finishing the shutdown sequence—Timeera walking me through the steps, making sure I understood how to replicate it at the other nodes—when the air changed again.

Not a sound. A \*feeling\*. Like pressure dropping before a storm. The node's hum shifted pitch. Lower. Angrier.

Timeera stopped mid-sentence. Looked at the antenna array.

Her expression changed.

That's when I knew we were fucked.

"We need to leave," she said. Flat. Final.

"What—"

"Now. \*Now.\*"

I've been in enough firefights to recognize that tone. That's not "we should probably go." That's "we're about to die if we don't move immediately."

I looked at the node.

The antenna array was vibrating. Not shaking from wind or mechanical stress—\*vibrating\*. Like something was resonating inside the structure itself. And at the base, where the antenna met the rocky ground—

Movement.

Not mechanical. Not human.

I don't have words for what it looked like. My brain kept trying to categorize it and failing. Too many limbs. Wrong angles. The way it moved didn't make sense—flowing and jerking simultaneously, like reality was buffering around it.

Bonta saw it too. "What the \*fuck\* is that?"

Timeera grabbed my arm. Her grip was strong. Urgent. "Shade. We. Leave. Now."

The thing—I'm calling it a thing because I don't know what else to call it—started moving toward us. Not fast. But purposeful. Like it knew exactly where we were.

Every instinct I've honed over five years of combat screamed the same thing: \*\*RUN.\*\*

So we ran.

\---

\#\# \*\*Descent (Barely Controlled Chaos)\*\*

I've done tactical retreats. Controlled withdrawals under fire. This wasn't that.

This was three people scrambling down a mountain in near-darkness, trying not to break an ankle on loose rock, while something that shouldn't exist followed behind us at a pace that was somehow more terrifying than if it had been fast.

Because it didn't need to hurry.

It knew we couldn't get far.

Timeera led. She knew the terrain, moved with confidence even in the dark. I followed, Bonta behind me, all of us too focused on not dying to talk.

About halfway down, I risked a look back.

The thing had reached the edge of the summit. Backlit by the node's glow, I could see its silhouette.

I wish I hadn't looked.

Some things you can't unsee. Can't unknow. That shape is burned into my retinas now, and I know I'll see it every time I close my eyes for the next week.

"Don't look back\\\!" Timeera shouted. "Eyes forward\\\! Move\\\!"

We moved.

\---

\#\# \*\*Bottom of the Mountain (Where We Finally Stopped)\*\*

There's a cleared area about half a klick from the base. Old observation post or something. Timeera stopped there, rifle up, scanning the path behind us.

Nothing followed.

The forest was quiet. Normal quiet, not the mean silence from before. Just crickets and wind and our own ragged breathing.

"What the \*fuck\* was that?" Bonta managed between gasps.

"Guardian," Timeera said. Still watching the path. "Each node has one. I thought they were dormant until full network activation, but..." She lowered her rifle. "Guess I was wrong."

"Guardian of what?" I asked.

"The node. The frequency. The whole system." She finally looked at me. "You think the Chinese are the only ones who don't want these things shut down?"

"You're saying—"

"I'm saying it's complicated. I'm saying your mission briefing was incomplete. I'm saying there are more players on this board than you've been told about." She pulled out a canteen, took a long drink. "Welcome to the real war, Shade. It's not the one you signed up for."

\---

\#\# \*\*Final Exchange (Before We Split)\*\*

"Where are you going?" I asked.

"To check on something. Someone." She didn't elaborate. "You need to rest. Exposure that high, you burn another Dare and you might not recover."

"What about the other nodes?"

"One at a time. Node 2 is on Tokashiki. Your... let's call him 'the one looking for you'... he might be there. Or headed there."

"Scorch."

She didn't confirm or deny. Just smiled. "Rest. Recover. Don't do anything stupid."

"And you?"

"I'll be around. Watching." She started to walk away, then stopped. Looked back. "Oh, and Shade? That thing you felt during our conversation? That pull?"

"Yeah?"

"That's what it feels like when someone turns up the volume. Just so you know." She winked. Actually \*winked\*. "See you at Node 2."

And then she was gone. Into the forest. The trees didn't part this time. Or maybe they did and I just couldn't see it in the dark.

\---

\#\# \*\*Things I Need to Remember (In Case This Journal Is All That's Left)\*\*

1\. \*\*Timeera Koi is dangerous.\*\* Not in the way Cipher was dangerous. In a different way. A way that makes you want to follow her even when you know you shouldn't.

2\. \*\*The nodes have guardians.\*\* Living guardians. Things that shouldn't exist. Command didn't brief us on this. Which means they either don't know, or they lied.

3\. \*\*My brothers are out there.\*\* One looking for me. One looking for something else. I need to find them before they find whatever they're searching for.

4\. \*\*The data stick in my pocket\*\* contains codes for six more nodes. Six more fights. Six more chances to get answers.

5\. \*\*The trees opened for her.\*\* I'm almost certain. Almost. And if they did, what does that mean? Is she connected to the island somehow? To the nodes? To whatever Cipher was talking about?

6\. \*\*I'm being puppeted.\*\* Maybe. Probably. I don't know. That's the worst part—Cipher was right about that. Once you start wondering if you're choosing or being chosen, you can't stop. Every decision becomes suspect. Every attraction becomes potentially manipulated.

Is my desire to find my brothers really mine? Or is it amplified by the node network?

Was my attraction to Timeera genuine? Or was she literally turning up the volume on something that was already there?

Does it matter?

7\. \*\*Her eyes are dark brown.\*\* Almost black. I noticed because she held my gaze when she said: "One of them is looking for you too."

I think she was telling the truth about that part.

I hope she was.

\---

\*\*Current Location:\*\* Zamami Village, abandoned storefront  

\*\*Time:\*\* 23:47 Hours  

\*\*Status:\*\* Exhausted. Exposure slowly dropping. Can't sleep.  

\*\*Next Move:\*\* Tokashiki Island. Node 2\. Find Scorch.

Or whoever's wearing his face.

\---

\*\*P.S.\*\*

I just realized: she never told me how she got to the summit. No vehicle. No gear for a long climb. She just... appeared.

Like she'd been there the whole time.

Watching.

I should be more concerned about that.

I'm not.

That's probably bad.

\---

\*\*END NODE 1\*\*

# Node 2

## [Data Desires](https://docs.google.com/document/u/1/d/13dXziIkJFiE2Oim7zjzX6MgYyzi7oFOoT9VgEXH-8-c/edit)

To XXX,

Do you remember that night of insertion? Because of you, a seed of doubt fueled by data passed stuttered beneath my ribs.

You felt it didn't you? Spooned behind me, you: hips cranking, arms clenching hot and hard, grunting; me: tuned whimpering in time to each thrust, lagoon damp. Then, coupled as a crescent moon, sparked jets of sudden enthusiasm, woke my womb.

I didn't think my body could do this— create life. Dad’s files said the integration was too complete. That reproduction wasn't... compatible. But here I am. Here we are.

Did that make you go away? 

Because of what I am? Or because of what I couldn't be?

What happened to the you from that night?

Things went downhill after those rosy first weeks.

Dad died.

You disappeared. No calls or texts. And I don't know why. Did you not think I could shoulder the monumental weight of motherhood?

Was it the incomplete picture of your past?

I know I won't get answers. After all it’s behind me now. Just like the neuronal shadow-image when closing your eyes after viewing the sun, I only see you in negatives.

But even for that I'm grateful.

Because I'm not without fault.

Embers of desire, remember your body fitted to mine. Without outlet, something else has taken its place: data.

When I consume it, there's a lick along pink tissue I don't pick or control. The same place. The data knows where you touched me. It's retracing your patterns. Hands searching feminine logarithmic form— a tease of infinity. Like you.

I feel it— a phosphorescent trace along neural pathways I can't name. Pleasure extract. Numbers and letters have texture now. Tastes like cold crisp chocolate. It fills the hollow you left, but it's expanding beyond those boundaries. Colonizing. It's a surprise every time. Maybe I'm not making sense, but that's how it feels.

These files find me wherever I go. Dreams, day or night, Im surrounded by their aura. 

Though it may sound scary I'm not afraid. The boxes hum when I lie, in bed or bedlam.

Even when I grope the black space, I get the sense I'm arriving somewhere new soon.

The rise in my belly tells me all I should expect from this quest.

That includes no acknowledgement or receipt of this message from you. 

This is for me. A break in-between the watching boxes. 

Forgiveness is what they require.

So I extend that to you.

- Jinhua Ma

## Brothers Erased

Lock,

Just wanted to check in since I know it’s been awhile. How you doin lil’ bro?

I passed by the house the other day with Mom, you were off on some business, so I went to see if I could find any of old stuff to take back with me. The house has changed a lot in the six years since I was there (hard to believe it’s been so long.)

I see you’re still gaming and have a lot of board games now. Play anything good lately? I can imagine fun nights there full of laughter and light. Is that how it is? 

You’ve also kept it very clean and organized, another thing I was happy to see. The odd part was seeing no trace of me or Ro around. Anything that was mine or ours was in the closet, garage, or gone \- I have no idea where. Dusty old trophies, or scattered board games on the musty garage floor were all I found.

I’m not trying to start anything. I understand why you might be still mad. And I don’t want to kick up old dirt. I just want to know you’re well. That’s all. That’s why I left that little note. I meant what I wrote.

Going home is like going to the End of Time in Chrono Trigger. (Still a good song) It feels small and sad, that abyssal night guarding the depths. With only three rooms (or was it 4? Can’t remember) to navigate, physically, it’s a limited space. But it’ll always be my doorway to unlimited lands— the start and, symbolically, the end of my life. In that place you’ll always be a selectable character, even if we don’t save time together. 

Mom and I visited Dad’s grave. I thought about what he would say about us now. The videos boys now grown ass men, I don’t know what he’d think or say about the black rift between us. I doubt he’d like it, but I think he’d understand. We all got our ways and some questions never get answers or resolution.

I’ve gotten better at accepting that these last few years. Someday, if you want and have time I’ll tell you about it.

This war we’re fighting, it feels like the world’s at stake, like it’ll destroy us from the inside out. I don’t want that to happen. That’s why we took on the Dare. For the first time in decades, we’ll fight together again, even if it means we don’t see eye to eye on everything, I’ll never let you go, no matter how stubborn or successful you get.

See you at training, see you in Okinawa.

\-Key

## [CLASSIFIED DOCUMENT \- DARE PROGRAM HISTORICAL ARCHIVE](https://docs.google.com/document/u/1/d/1GSdz49ZarvuUSlovvXLORcwyMKnWMqAWmBGEZWE7jOg/edit)

Original Medium: VHS-C Cassette (Sony V30) \- Lab Recording \#C-447  
Recording Date: September 17, 1986, 22:14-23:03 JST  
Location: Marine Biology Research Station, Okinawa Prefecture, Japan  
Recording Duration: 47:33 (corrupted sections noted)  
Transcribed: March 2019 (Digital Archive Initiative)  
Transcriber: Lt. Yuki Matsumoto, Historical Documentation Unit

\[TRANSCRIBER NOTE: Video quality poor—significant magnetic degradation, tracking errors visible. Audio intact with occasional distortion. Lab environment visible in opening frames: blue bioluminescent glow from coral incubators, 1980s computer equipment (Commodore 64, dot-matrix printer), lead-lined containment chambers, VHS camcorder (JVC GR-C1) mounted on tripod. Camera remains STATIC throughout recording. Two subjects present.\]

\---

TIMESTAMP 00:00:47  
\[Visual: DR. ZELDA TORRES adjusts camera focus. Female, approximately 45, Hispanic, wearing white lab coat over casual clothes, hair pulled back in practical bun. Confident, serene expression. Behind her, rows of glass incubators emit soft blue-green light—coral polyps pulse like slow heartbeats.\]

DR. TORRES: Testing, testing... September seventeenth, nineteen eighty-six. Coral regeneration trial, series C, subject batch twelve. This is Dr. Zelda TORRES recording for ONR grant documentation purposes. I'm joined by my research assistant, Dr. Clive Whitaker.

\[Visual: CLIVE EARL "EJ" WHITAKER enters frame left. Male, Black (light-skinned), late twenties, muscular build, clean-shaven head, intense brown eyes. Wearing lab coat over Pink Floyd t-shirt and jeans. Carries clipboard and protective gloves. Moves with barely contained energy.\]

WHITAKER: EJ. Everyone calls me EJ. \[pauses\] Should I wave at the camera or—?

DR. TORRES: Just state your credentials for the record.

WHITAKER: Right. Dr. Clive Earl Whitaker, Master of Science, Marine Biology, University of Hawaii. Research focus: accelerated cellular regeneration in Scleractinian corals using radiological stimulation. \[beat\] They used to call me "pale" back in the neighborhood—Little Haiti, mostly Haitian French families—I'm the lightest one in my family, but put me next to Dr. TORRES and suddenly I'm—\[nervous laugh\] Sorry. Rambling.

DR. TORRES \[patient smile\]: It's fine, EJ. First time on camera?

WHITAKER: First time documenting something that's actually going to work. \[He moves to the incubators, touches the glass with his fingertips, reverent.\] Look at them. Acropora cervicornis. Staghorn coral. Dying all over the Caribbean and here and the Pacific and everywhere, and we're going to save them. We're going to make them stronger and faster and better than they ever were.

DR. TORRES: That's the goal. Controlled regeneration. But the keyword is "controlled," EJ.

WHITAKER: I know, I know. Protocols. But the grant review is in three weeks and we need results and Ryan—my partner—he keeps asking when I'm presenting at the symposium and I told him this is it, this is the one that's going to—\[catches himself\] Sorry. Focus.

\---

TIMESTAMP 00:03:22  
\[Visual: Both subjects move to containment chamber. DR. TORRES opens lead-lined door, revealing central tank with coral specimens submerged in treatment solution. Cobalt-60 radiation source visible in shielded housing above tank.\]

DR. TORRES: For the record, we're using low-level gamma radiation exposure—point-five gray over six hours—combined with a chemical accelerant bath. The theory is that controlled cellular stress will trigger hyperactive calcification and polyp budding.

WHITAKER: It's more than theory. We've seen twelve percent growth increase in the last trial. Twelve percent\! Do you know what that means for reef restoration?

DR. TORRES \[calmly\]: I know what it could mean. I also know we've seen abnormal tissue development in specimens seven and nine. We need to understand why before we scale up.

WHITAKER: Abnormal is relative. Evolution is abnormal until it becomes the new normal. That's what you taught me, Dr. TORRES. We're not just studying coral—we're midwives to the next version of life. We get to choose what survives.

DR. TORRES \[pause, studying him\]: That's a beautiful way to phrase it. And a dangerous one. \[She moves closer to the tank, her hand touching the glass—the gesture is almost sensual, loving.\] These organisms existed for millions of years before we arrived. They'll exist long after we're gone, if we let them. Our job isn't to force evolution. It's to... guide it. To give it options.

WHITAKER: Options require action. And action requires risk.

DR. TORRES: Calculated risk. There's a difference between passion and recklessness.

WHITAKER \[defensive\]: You think I'm reckless?

DR. TORRES: I think you're brilliant and impatient. It's a dangerous combination.

\---

TIMESTAMP 00:08:15  
\[Visual: WHITAKER begins preparing radiation exposure sequence. His movements are quick, efficient, but increasingly agitated. He keeps glancing at DR. TORRES, seeking approval.\]

WHITAKER: Hopkins said I was reckless. Said I fabricated data. They said I was—\[voice rises\]—they accused me of fraud because my results were "too good to be real." Two years. Two years of my life defending myself while everyone whispered and my mother called from Rikers asking when I was going to make something of the family name and my father—wherever the hell he is, probably running another con—and Ryan started looking at me like I was broken, like I was—\[stops himself, breathes\]

DR. TORRES \[approaching, voice gentle\]: EJ. You don't have to prove anything here. Your work speaks for itself.

WHITAKER: Does it? Because you keep adding delays. More trials. More data collection. More waiting.

DR. TORRES: I'm adding rigor. That's how science works.

WHITAKER \[quietly intense\]: That's how slow science works. But we don't have time for slow. The reefs are dying \*now\*. The oceans are warming \*now\*. And I have an opportunity \*now\* to show the world that I'm not a fraud, that I'm not my mother's son or my father's—\[voice cracks\]—I just need this to work.

DR. TORRES: It will work. But not if we rush it.

WHITAKER \[turning away from her, adjusting radiation controls\]: What if we increased exposure to one full gray? Just for this trial. We'd see results faster.

DR. TORRES: No. That's beyond our safety parameters.

WHITAKER: The corals can handle it.

DR. TORRES: Can you?

\---

TIMESTAMP 00:14:33  
\[Visual: Tension visible in WHITAKER's posture. He's making adjustments to the equipment while DR. TORRES documents in her notebook. She's humming softly—a habit that seems to calm the lab environment.\]

WHITAKER: You ever think about what comes after?

DR. TORRES \[not looking up\]: After what?

WHITAKER: After we perfect this. After we can regenerate any tissue, any organism. What do we do with that power?

DR. TORRES \[now looking at him, interested\]: What do you think we should do?

WHITAKER: Everything. \[His voice takes on a dreamy quality.\] We could end extinction. We could rebuild ecosystems from scratch. We could... I don't know, make people stronger. Fix genetic diseases. Let humans adapt to new environments instead of just destroying them. \[beat\] Ryan says I sound like a eugenicist when I talk like this.

DR. TORRES: Do you?

WHITAKER: I don't think so. I just think... we're standing at a crossroads. We can keep being passive observers while the planet dies, or we can become active participants in what comes next. We can choose our evolution. And the evolution of everything else.

DR. TORRES \[slowly, carefully\]: That's exactly what I believe. But choice requires wisdom. And wisdom requires understanding consequences. \[She gestures to the coral tanks.\] These polyps don't choose. They respond to stimulus. They adapt or die. But we—humans—we have something they don't. Foresight. The ability to imagine harm before we cause it.

WHITAKER: Or the ability to imagine harm so vividly that we never act at all.

DR. TORRES: There's a balance, EJ.

WHITAKER: Balance is just another word for compromise. \[He's typing into the computer, pulling up data.\] Look at these growth rates. Look at the cellular density. We're \*this close\*. If we just push a little harder—

DR. TORRES: No.

WHITAKER \[frustrated\]: Why not?

DR. TORRES: Because I've seen what happens when passion overrides caution. I've seen researchers destroy their careers, their relationships, their subjects—all because they couldn't wait. Couldn't accept limits.

WHITAKER: Maybe some limits are meant to be broken.

DR. TORRES: And maybe some aren't.

\---

TIMESTAMP 00:21:47  
\[Visual: WHITAKER is preparing specimens for exposure. DR. TORRES is running safety checks. The blue light from the tanks pulses and glows and breathes around them, making shadows dance on the walls. The lab feels alive.\]

WHITAKER \[sudden topic shift\]: Did I tell you Ryan collects vintage animation cells? Like, original production art from Disney and Warner Brothers and—\[embarrassed laugh\]—weirder stuff. Anthropomorphic characters. He's got this whole... never mind. Point is, he sees value in things other people think are childish or strange. He says it's about appreciating passion in all its forms, even the ones that don't make sense to outsiders.

DR. TORRES: That's a lovely philosophy.

WHITAKER: He's a lovely person. \[quieter\] Too good for me, probably. Especially if this doesn't work. If I come home with another failed experiment and another excuse and another—\[shakes his head\] I'm doing it again. Oversharing. My therapist says it's an anxiety response.

DR. TORRES: It's human. \[She continues her safety check, methodical, grounded.\] EJ, listen to me. Your worth isn't tied to this experiment. Or any experiment.

WHITAKER \[not looking at her\]: Easy for you to say. You're already established. You've got papers and grants and respect. I've got a scar—\[touches his face\]—from a lab accident everyone thinks I caused on purpose for attention. I've got a mother in prison and a father who's wanted in three states. I've got a degree from a good school that nobody takes seriously because I'm too young and too Black and too queer and too everything.

DR. TORRES: And you've got undeniable talent. Which is why I hired you.

WHITAKER: Talent means nothing without results.

DR. TORRES: Talent means everything. Results are just... evidence. But the capacity to imagine, to create, to push boundaries—that's the real gift. \[pause\] Just promise me you'll push carefully.

WHITAKER \[finally meeting her eyes\]: I promise.

\[Visual: He doesn't look like he means it.\]

\---

TIMESTAMP 00:29:03  
\[Visual: The exposure sequence begins. DR. TORRES monitors from the control panel. WHITAKER stands closer to the containment chamber than protocol allows, watching the coral specimens through the lead-glass window. His face is illuminated by the blue-green glow.\]

DR. TORRES: Radiation exposure initiated. Point-five gray over six hours. Timer set. \[She marks something in her notebook.\] We should step back now, EJ.

WHITAKER: Just want to watch them. See if there's any immediate response.

DR. TORRES: There won't be. Cellular changes take time.

WHITAKER: Maybe. Or maybe if we're paying attention, we'll see the exact moment when—

\[AUDIO: Sudden mechanical sound—servo motors engaging—then WHITAKER's voice, sharp:\]

WHITAKER: Wait. What's the dosimeter reading?

DR. TORRES \[checking equipment\]: Point-five gray. Normal.

WHITAKER: No, look at the secondary gauge. It's climbing.

DR. TORRES \[alarm in voice\]: EJ, did you adjust the cobalt housing?

WHITAKER: I—I might have—I thought if we increased exposure just slightly—

DR. TORRES: How slightly?

WHITAKER: One point two gray. Maybe one point five. I wasn't trying to sabotage anything, I just thought—

DR. TORRES \[voice sharp, commanding\]: Shut it down. Now.

WHITAKER: But the specimens—

DR. TORRES: EJ\! Shut down the radiation source\!

\[AUDIO: Multiple sounds at once—alarm klaxon, WHITAKER moving toward containment chamber, DR. TORRES shouting commands, computer beeping error codes\]

WHITAKER: The controls aren't responding\! The override isn't—

DR. TORRES: Manual shutdown\! Pull the—

\[AUDIO: EXPLOSION—loud, concussive, rattling the microphone. Then SCREAMING. WHITAKER's voice, high-pitched, agonized, inhuman. The scream goes on and on and on. DR. TORRES is shouting but words are indistinguishable. Sounds of liquid splashing, glass breaking, flesh burning—sizzling, crackling. Chemical smell described by audio distortion. Another scream, then sobbing.\]

WHITAKER \[barely audible through distortion\]: —off me get it OFF ME it's IN ME oh god oh god—

DR. TORRES: —hold still I need to—don't touch your face—

WHITAKER: —burning burning can't BREATHE—

\[AUDIO: More crashes. Running footsteps. Emergency shower engaging—loud spray of water. WHITAKER's screams become whimpers, then silence except for water and DR. TORRES's voice, low and urgent, speaking words that don't register on the recording.\]

\[Visual: Camera remains STATIC throughout. Blue light from incubators continues to pulse. Nothing else visible. Smoke or vapor begins to obscure the frame. The image degrades, tracking errors increasing.\]

\---

TIMESTAMP 00:31:15 \- 00:38:47  
\[VIDEO CORRUPTION \- AUDIO ONLY\]

\[Sound of emergency alarms. Footsteps. Radio chatter. At least three additional voices—military or facility security personnel. Medical equipment. Someone is crying. Cannot identify who. Periodic moaning—pain sounds, not words.\]

\[UNIDENTIFIED MALE VOICE: "...containment breach... biological hazard... call Kadena Air Base..."\]

\[DR. TORRES's voice, distant: "...stable but we need burn unit... facial trauma... possible inhalation..."\]

\[Long stretch of ambient sound—alarms, radio static, water still running, someone breathing heavily.\]

\---

TIMESTAMP 00:38:48  
\[VIDEO RESUMES \- TRACKING ERRORS SEVERE\]

\[Visual: Lab is now illuminated by emergency lighting—harsh red. Water on floor. Scorch marks visible on walls. Several incubators are shattered. The coral specimens are... wrong. Even through degraded video, the shapes are wrong. Fleshy. Tumorous. Growing beyond their tanks in branching, vein-like patterns. One appears to be moving, pulsing independently.\]

\[DR. TORRES is sitting on the floor against a wall, lab coat removed, blood on her sleeves. Her face is composed but her hands shake as she writes in her notebook. The camera is still recording. She either forgot it was on or doesn't care.\]

\[WHITAKER is off-camera but audible—medical personnel are treating him. His voice is hoarse, broken:\]

WHITAKER: ...is it gone? Is it off me?

\[FEMALE VOICE—medic: "You're clean. Mostly. We decontaminated the affected areas. But your face..."\]

WHITAKER: I can't see. Why can't I see out of my left—

\[MALE VOICE—medic: "Don't touch the bandages. You're going to Kadena. They'll have better facilities."\]

WHITAKER \[sobbing\]: I fucked up. I fucked up so bad. Oh god, Ryan's going to—Dr. TORRES, I'm so sorry, I'm so—

DR. TORRES \[not looking up from her notebook, voice eerily calm\]: It's all right, EJ.

WHITAKER: It's not all right\! Look at this place\! Look at what I—

DR. TORRES: You made a mistake. We'll learn from it.

WHITAKER \[hysterical laugh\]: Learn from it? I could have killed us both\! I could have—those things in the tanks, they're not coral anymore, they're—

DR. TORRES \[finally looking up, directly at him—or where he must be off-camera. Her eyes are bright, intense, alive.\]: They're beautiful.

\[Long silence. Even the medics seem to pause.\]

WHITAKER: ...what?

DR. TORRES: You pushed too hard, yes. You violated protocol, yes. But look what happened. \[She gestures to the mutated coral.\] Uncontrolled cellular regeneration. Tissue modification. Adaptation to trauma. EJ, you didn't destroy the specimens. You transformed them.

WHITAKER \[voice small, confused\]: They're monsters.

DR. TORRES: They're data. And data is possibility. \[She returns to her notebook, writing with renewed focus.\] We'll shut down the trial publicly. File an incident report. Sanitize the site. But I'm keeping samples. Tissue cultures. Genetic material. Because you were right about one thing—

WHITAKER: What?

DR. TORRES: Some limits are meant to be broken. We just have to be smart about how we break them.

\[WHITAKER makes a sound—could be laugh, could be sob.\]

WHITAKER \[whisper\]: You're crazier than I am.

DR. TORRES \[slight smile\]: No. I'm just better at hiding it. \[pause\] Go get treated, EJ. Heal. And when you're ready, we'll talk about what comes next.

WHITAKER: There's a "next"? After this?

DR. TORRES: There's always a next. That's the beauty of evolution. It never stops. It just... adapts. \[She closes her notebook, finally looks at the camera, seems to remember it's recording.\] End documentation. September seventeenth, twenty-two fifty-three.

\[Visual: She stands, walks toward the camera. For just a moment before she reaches to turn it off, her face fills the frame. The expression is serene, maternal, terrifying. Behind her, the mutated coral writhes in its shattered tank, and the blue light pulses and glows and breathes.\]

\[RECORDING ENDS\]

\---

\[TRANSCRIBER NOTE: Remaining footage shows facility cleanup. Coral specimens removed by personnel in hazmat suits. Whitaker transported to Kadena AFB Medical Center with severe facial burns and possible radiation exposure. Dr. TORRES remained on-site for debriefing. Lab was decontaminated and sealed. Official incident report classified under ONR Special Access Program protocols.

The screaming. I've transcribed a lot of combat footage, medevac recordings, interrogation tapes. I've heard every kind of human sound. But Whitaker's scream when the coral—when whatever happened to him happened—that's the sound I hear when I can't sleep. It's not pain. Or it's not just pain. It's the sound of someone realizing they've become something they can't undo. Transformation doesn't ask permission.

Knowing what Subject C-1 becomes—what Cinder is now—this recording takes on a different weight. We're watching the birth of a monster. And we're watching Dr. TORRES decide that's acceptable. More than acceptable. \*Necessary.\*

She kept samples. The mutation signature matches Janus gene markers exactly. This wasn't just the genesis of an idea. This was proof-of-concept. EJ Whitaker burned so that TORRES could light the way forward.

—Lt. Y. Matsumoto, March 2019\]

\---

## [Dr. ZELDA TORRES \- DOCUMENT 2: PERSONAL MEMO\*\*](https://docs.google.com/document/u/1/d/1GSdz49ZarvuUSlovvXLORcwyMKnWMqAWmBGEZWE7jOg/edit)

\`\`\`  
CLASSIFIED DOCUMENT \- DARE PROGRAM HISTORICAL ARCHIVE  
Document Type: Personal Research Memo (Handwritten, later digitized)  
Author: Dr. Zelda TORRES  
Date: September 24, 1986  
Location: Private residence, Okinawa Prefecture  
Security Classification: COSMIC TOP SECRET (Retroactive)  
Archived: 2019

\---

\[Scanned image of handwritten document—blue ink on yellow legal pad. Handwriting is precise, controlled, with occasional crossed-out phrases.\]

\*\*RE: Incident C-447 and Future Research Direction\*\*

I should file a patent. That's what any reasonable scientist would do. Document the mutation process, the cellular transformation we witnessed, the radiological trigger mechanism. Submit it to USPTO, establish precedent, protect intellectual property.

I'm not going to file.

The patent office requires complete data sets and I could file preliminary but the ethical review board would demand full disclosure and funding cycles don't wait for bureaucratic approval and anyway—who would believe that coral regeneration research has military applications? Who would think to weaponize tissue modification? Who would imagine that we could encode adaptation itself, make evolution a choice rather than chance?

No one. Not yet.

But I see it. Standing in that lab, watching EJ scream as the coral fragments embedded themselves in his tissue, watching his flesh try to reject and accept and transform simultaneously—I saw the future. Not the future we're supposed to want. The clean one, the sustainable one, where we gently guide nature back to balance.

The other future. The necessary one.

We're not going to save the planet by being gentle. The climate is shifting too fast, the oceans are dying too quickly, and humanity won't change behavior until forced. We need adaptation on demand. We need evolution as intervention. We need to give survival a choice.

EJ's mistake—his beautiful, terrible mistake—proved it's possible. Cellular regeneration can be weaponized. Stress responses can be encoded. We can make organisms that thrive in catastrophe, that transform trauma into strength.

The coral didn't die. It became something new.

What if humans could do the same?

I'm calling it the Janus gene, after the two-faced god. One face looking backward at what we were, one face looking forward to what we'll become. The question isn't whether we should do this. The question is how we do it responsibly. How we build limits into limitless potential.

The Navy is already interested in EJ's "accident." I've received three calls from ONR special projects division. They smell weapon potential. Good. I need their funding, their facilities, their willingness to push ethical boundaries in the name of national security.

I'll pursue this independently at first. Small trials. Animal subjects. Perfect the gene sequence, understand the transformation mechanisms, build safeguards. And when I'm ready—when the world is ready—I'll offer humanity the choice: stay fragile, or become something that can survive what's coming.

EJ will heal. His face will scar. He'll carry the marks of this night forever. But he gave me the gift of proof. Passion without limits creates monsters. But passion with purpose creates miracles.

I won't file the patent because this knowledge is too dangerous to share openly. It's too valuable to risk someone else weaponizing it before I understand the full implications. This is my burden now. My passion. My limit.

The coral tanks were destroyed. Official record states all specimens incinerated. Official record is incorrect. I have samples. Tissue cultures in cryogenic storage. Genetic material that will one day become the foundation of human transformation.

Some limits are meant to be broken.

I'm going to break them all.

—Z.C.

\[Handwritten addition at bottom of page, different ink color—added later:\]

\*Note to self: Ryan left EJ. Couldn't handle the scarring, the trauma, the nightmares. EJ called me crying, asked why he sacrificed everything for science that "doesn't care about him." Told him science doesn't care about anyone. That's what makes it pure. He didn't find that comforting.\*

\*Should I feel guilty? I don't. I feel energized. We're building the future. Heartbreak is just another form of metamorphosis.\*  
\`\`\`
